Data engineering work differs depending on the industry and the company. Typically data engineering handles most of the plumbing for data, this could be realtime events from various applications, websites, internet of things. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1137284211334709288 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1137284211334709288><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105332965977944064/a3f1c0674bd7d1e2c448aa3431f34fc3.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=julmust data-user-id=105332965977944064>Julmust</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, August 5, 2023 4:21 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1137284211334709288>8/5/2023 4:21 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;d definitely call that a basic ETL pipeline. You&#39;re Extracting (scraping), Transforming (cleaning/organizing), and Loading it into a db.

I&#39;d suggest you look into ELT as well. In that case you extract the data and load it into a db right away before doing your transformations in SQL. For this it helps if the data is more structured so see if you can find any like API data to ingest.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1139730737566855209 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1139730737566855209><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/114858490555531268/746e25b5e6bc3e73f5a5e166568b153b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=apatheticlamp data-user-id=114858490555531268>Lamp - Databricks #1 fan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, August 11, 2023 10:23 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1139730737566855209>8/11/2023 10:23 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;m not 100% confident in my answer, but I think the answer is <em>potentially sometimes</em>
Assuming that you are querying a relational database, both spark and presto have the latency of reading the data from the database first, I/O can be slow
Spark and Presto however had the ability to massive scale your compute, you could have Spark chunk your reads in parallel and then have 10x the compute power in the spark cluster than the relational database might be</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1139730824804184108 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1139730824804184108><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, August 11, 2023 10:23 PM">10:23 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>so depending on your workload, I think the answer is <em>maybe</em></span></div></div></div></div></div>

I want to do a scrapper for GPU prices. I already get all the scraping job done, but I have problems with database design.

I wanted to create three tables: Shop (details of on-line shops that i am scraping), GraphicCard (detail about GPU model) and Price (datetime, price, shop_id, gpu_id). My problem is that for some online shops I can&#39;t get both EAN number and producent code (sometimes there is none of them available, only &#39;name of product&#39;). Because of that I think I need to create unique ID for every GPU from auto-increment to have a primary key. 

But it complicates so much inserting new data to Price table. I would need to find gpu_ID by quering GraphicCard table first. 

Maybe there is some obvious solution or clever work-around that an experienced person just see immediately after reading that and would want to give some advices?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1141701100005769226 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1141701100005769226><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/243951995709292544/d5dc91eb57eeb02fbf37da2088cf6e2c.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=majyphy data-user-id=243951995709292544>Majy</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, August 17, 2023 8:52 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1141701100005769226>8/17/2023 8:52 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Can you scrap without defining this ID, and then at a later stage (in a view or something) regroup them with EAN number and/or producent code? The rest we&#39;ll teach them. So focus on getting really good at both. For Python knowing stuff like generators, list comprehension, and object oriented programming are all good indicators of a decent knowledge. For SQL it&#39;s stuff like CTE&#39;s, window functions, joins.

Also just learn how to write code. In my college days the focus was solely on &quot;does it run?&quot; not &quot;is it maintainable/readable?&quot; or &quot;is it structured correctly?&quot; and the two latter are just as important. For this you can have a look at open source projects.

Bonus points:
<ul><li>Learning best practices and design patterns</li><li>Read up on distributed computing</li><li>Understanding of OLTP vs. OLAP</li><li>Tech: Airflow / dbt / Docker / Kafka (or any other queue system)</li></ul></span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=bulb><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💡 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4a1.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

2:42 AM">2:42 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><a class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://stackoverflow.com/questions/55248030/run-a-spark-job-python-vs-spark-submit><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Run a spark job: python vs spark.submit</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">The common way of running a spark job appears to be using spark-submit as below (source):

spark-submit --py-files pyfile.py,zipfile.zip main.py --arg1 val1
Being newer to spark, I wanted to know ...</div></div></div><div class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-container><a class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-link href=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/VbfwnzN2MM794XNccNxDzrB1YeuPrxR53y11bwRfflY/%3Fv%3D73d79a89bded/https/cdn.sstatic.net/Sites/stackoverflow/Img/apple-touch-icon%402.png> <img class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail src=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/VbfwnzN2MM794XNccNxDzrB1YeuPrxR53y11bwRfflY/%3Fv%3D73d79a89bded/https/cdn.sstatic.net/Sites/stackoverflow/Img/apple-touch-icon%402.png alt=Thumbnail loading=lazy> </a></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1146331851724693515 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1146331851724693515><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/766658694057951252/caa35da3b49a6cff9e9bdbca92bd9da1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=phat_pro data-user-id=766658694057951252>Alley</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, August 30, 2023 3:33 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1146331851724693515>8/30/2023 3:33 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>But we can adjust the configurations in app.py to connect to cluster and run <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">python app.py</code>  instead of <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">spark-submit</code></span></div></div></div></div></div>

Our current architecture currently is simple: Oracle data warehouse --&gt; SAS server; data to be used by analysts.

As we plan to shift to another tool, an issue we are facing is how simple it is to save and load data in SAS for non-tech people. It&#39;s all UI.

At t=1: read data from node B and C
At t=2: write replicates to node B and C

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1152564181803995136 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1152564181803995136><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/766658694057951252/caa35da3b49a6cff9e9bdbca92bd9da1.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=phat_pro>Alley</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1152560222691414126')"> So it still guarantee strong consistency when write and read simultaneously and write is not replicated yet to other nodes? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=philliphenry data-user-id=462278067474137088>PhillHenry</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, September 16, 2023 8:18 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1152564181803995136>9/16/2023 8:18 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Note, strong consistency means the reader sees the latest data. But what is the latest data is subtle. Again IIRC, if a third update comes in at the point where your description ends, and if nodes B and C agree that data=3, the cluster will never be in a state (from the point of view of a reader using CL of quorum) of data ever being 2. (Though it might for a reader using a less strict CL).</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1153033606336348250 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1153033606336348250><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=sammysevens777 data-user-id=833941249362493450>SamSon</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, September 17, 2023 3:23 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1153033606336348250>9/17/2023 3:23 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hi all -

I am developing an architecture to:
<ul><li>remotely manage fleets of servers and run bash scripts + test scripts against them
<ul><li>aggregating that data into a python pipeline to etl &amp; store onto a mysql db</li></ul><ul><li>design a GUI for users to run tests against servers in the network</li></ul>
One question i have - i would really like to move to more db storage, and away from file storagr for a few things:
<ul><li>tests can run for &gt;3 days, and i want to write test states to a table as a state machine, so a server can resume testing from when it failed</li></ul><ul><li>autonegotiate servers in the network, and write their ip info to a row in a db. When connecting to servers, this table should contain all info. This table will also be read in by the GUI, so users can see which servers are &quot;online&quot;.</li></ul>
I think dbs are very underused where i work, and will also enable broader use cases (and simplify data collection as well)</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, September 17, 2023 3:24 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
